loose
NOTE ON USAGE ÓÃ·¨: The adjective loose has several senses. ĞÎÈİ´ÊlooseÓĞ¼¸¸öÒåÏî. Two of these are 1 `not tied up' and 2 `not tight' ÆäÖĞÁ½ÏîÊÇ1Î´Ë©×¡µÄ, 2²»½ôµÄ: The dogs are loose in the garden. ¹·ÔÚ»¨Ô°Àï¶¼Ã»Ë©Öø. *  a tight/loose shirt, dress, belt, etc ½ôÉíµÄ[¿íËÉµÄ]³ÄÉÀ¡¢ Á¬ÒÂÈ¹¡¢ Æ¤´øµÈ. The verb loose (also unloose) relates to the first sense and means `set free' ¶¯´Êloose£¨¼°unloose£©ÓëµÚÒ»ÒåÓĞ¹Ø, ÒâÎª£àÊ¹²»ÊÜÔ¼Êø£§: The guard loosed the dogs when the burglar alarm went off. ·ÀµÁ¾¯±¨Æ÷Ò»Ïì, ¾¯ÎÀ¾Í·Å³öÁË¾¯È®. The verb loosen (also unloosen) relates to the second sense and means `make loose' ¶¯´Êloosen£¨¼°unloosen£©ÓëµÚ¶şÒåÓĞ¹Ø, ÒâÎª£àÊ¹ËÉ¿ª£§: After the huge meal he loosened his belt and went to sleep. Ëû±¥²ÍÒ»¶ÙÒÔáá¾ÍËÉ¿ªÑü´øË¯ÖøÁË. Note that the verb lose (pt lost, pp lost) is unconnected with loose or loosen. ×¢Òâ, ¶¯´Êlose£¨¹ıÈ¥Ê½lost, ¹ıÈ¥·Ö´Êlost£©Óëloose»òloosenÎŞ¹Ø.

loose
NOTE ON USAGE ÓÃ·¨: The adjective loose has several senses. ĞÎÈİ´ÊlooseÓĞ¼¸¸öÒåÏî. Two of these are 1 `not tied up' and 2 `not tight' ÆäÖĞÁ½ÏîÊÇ1Î´Ë©×¡µÄ, 2²»½ôµÄ: The dogs are loose in the garden. ¹·ÔÚ»¨Ô°Àï¶¼Ã»Ë©Öø. *  a tight/loose shirt, dress, belt, etc ½ôÉíµÄ[¿íËÉµÄ]³ÄÉÀ¡¢ Á¬ÒÂÈ¹¡¢ Æ¤´øµÈ. The verb loose (also unloose) relates to the first sense and means `set free' ¶¯´Êloose£¨¼°unloose£©ÓëµÚÒ»ÒåÓĞ¹Ø, ÒâÎª£àÊ¹²»ÊÜÔ¼Êø£§: The guard loosed the dogs when the burglar alarm went off. ·ÀµÁ¾¯±¨Æ÷Ò»Ïì, ¾¯ÎÀ¾Í·Å³öÁË¾¯È®.
